Theoretical Limits of Language Model Alignment
Authors: Lucas Monteiro Paes, Natalie Mackraz, Barry-John Theobald, Federico Danieli
First: 2026-05-08T01:32:22+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-08T01:32:22+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Language model (LM) alignment improves model outputs to reflect human preferences while preserving the capabilities of the base model. The most common alignment approaches are (i) reinforcement learning, which maximizes the expected reward under a KL-divergence constraint, and (ii) best-of-$N$ alignment, which selects the highest-reward output among $N$ independent samples. Despite their widespread use, the fundamental limits of reward improvement under a KL budget remain poorly understood. We characterize the information-theoretic limits of KL-regularized alignment by deriving the maximum achievable expected reward gain for a fixed KL-divergence budget. Our first result provides a closed-form expression for the optimal reward improvement, governed by a Jeffreys divergence term rather than the $\sqrt{\texttt{KL}}$ used in prior analyses. We further reformulate this expression as a covariance under the base model, yielding a practical estimator that predicts achievable alignment gains from base model samples alone. We extend our analysis to the proxy reward setting, showing that the gap between ideal and proxy alignment (reward hacking) grows with the magnitude of reward error and when the KL penalty factor decreases. We then prove that reward ensembling mitigates reward hacking, providing a theoretical justification for this technique used in practice. Empirically, we compute the KL-reward Pareto frontier for two tasks for LMs, safety and summarization, and show that best-of-$N$ closely approaches the theoretical limit, while PPO and GRPO remain substantially suboptimal. Our theoretical results shed light on several empirically observed phenomena in the alignment literature and suggest that algorithmic improvements are needed to achieve optimal alignment without high inference costs.
中文标题/摘要
标题：语言模型对齐的理论极限
语言模型（LM）对齐改善模型输出，使其反映人类偏好，同时保留基础模型的能力。最常见的对齐方法是（i）强化学习，在KL散度约束下最大化期望奖励，以及（ii）最佳$N$对齐，从$N$个独立样本中选择最高奖励输出。尽管这些方法被广泛使用，但在KL预算下奖励改善的基本极限仍然不甚了解。我们通过推导固定KL散度预算下可实现的最大期望奖励增益，来表征KL正则化对齐的信息论极限。我们的第一个结果提供了最优奖励改善的封闭形式表达式，该表达式由Jeffreys散度项主导，而不是先前分析中使用的$\sqrt{\texttt{KL}}$。我们进一步将该表达式重新表述为基础模型下的协方差，得出一个实用的估计器，仅通过基础模型样本预测可实现的对齐增益。我们将分析扩展到代理奖励设置，表明理想对齐与代理对齐（奖励黑客）之间的差距随着奖励误差的大小和KL惩罚因子的减少而增加。然后我们证明奖励集成可以减轻奖励黑客，为这一实践中使用的技术提供理论依据。通过实证，我们计算了两个任务（安全性和摘要）的KL-奖励帕累托前沿，并显示最佳$N$接近理论极限，而PPO和GRPO仍然显著次优。我们的理论结果阐明了对齐文献中观察到的几种经验现象，并建议需要算法改进以在不高推理成本的情况下实现最优对齐。
Summary / 总结
This paper addresses the challenges of aligning language models (LMs) with human preferences while maintaining their capabilities, highlighting the limitations of existing methods such as reinforcement learning and best-of-$N$ alignment. Previous approaches have not fully understood the fundamental limits of reward improvement under a KL-divergence constraint, leading to suboptimal performance. The authors propose a new theoretical framework that characterizes the information-theoretic limits of KL-regularized alignment, providing a closed-form expression for optimal reward improvement based on Jeffreys divergence. This methodology allows for practical estimations of achievable alignment gains and demonstrates that reward ensembling can mitigate reward hacking. The empirical results show that best-of-$N$ alignment closely approaches theoretical limits for tasks like safety and summarization, while traditional methods like PPO and GRPO are significantly less effective, indicating a need for algorithmic advancements to optimize alignment without incurring high inference costs.
本文探讨了如何在保持语言模型（LM）原有能力的同时，使其输出符合人类偏好的对齐问题，并指出现有方法（如强化学习和最佳$N$对齐）在KL散度预算下的奖励提升限制尚未得到充分理解。提出的方法引入了一种新的信息论框架，推导出基于Jeffreys散度的最优奖励提升的闭式表达，而不是之前使用的$\sqrt{\texttt{KL}}$，并将其重新表述为一种协方差估计器，以预测基模型样本的对齐增益。该论文通过提供对LM对齐限制的理论见解，并展示奖励集成可以缓解奖励黑客等问题，为该领域做出了贡献。在安全性和摘要任务上的实证评估表明，最佳$N$对齐接近理论极限，而传统方法如PPO和GRPO的效果显著低于最佳$N$，这表明需要算法改进以在不增加高推理成本的情况下优化对齐。
When No Benchmark Exists: Validating Comparative LLM Safety Scoring Without Ground-Truth Labels
Authors: Sushant Gautam, Finn Schwall, Annika Willoch Olstad, Fernando Vallecillos Ruiz, Birk Torpmann-Hagen, Sunniva Maria Stordal Bjørklund, Leon Moonen, Klas Pettersen, Michael A. Riegler
First: 2026-05-07T17:56:41+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-07T17:56:41+00:00
Comments: SimpleAudit Repository: https://github.com/kelkalot/simpleaudit
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Many deployments must compare candidate language models for safety before a labeled benchmark exists for the relevant language, sector, or regulatory regime. We formalize this setting as benchmarkless comparative safety scoring and specify the contract under which a scenario-based audit can be interpreted as deployment evidence. Scores are valid only under a fixed scenario pack, rubric, auditor, judge, sampling configuration, and rerun budget. Because no labels are available, we replace ground-truth agreement with an instrumental-validity chain: responsiveness to a controlled safe-versus-abliterated contrast, dominance of target-driven variance over auditor and judge artifacts, and stability across reruns. We instantiate the chain in SimpleAudit, a local-first scoring instrument, and validate it on a Norwegian safety pack. Safe and abliterated targets separate with AUROC values between 0.89 and 1.00, target identity is the dominant variance component ($η^2 \approx 0.52$), and severity profiles stabilize by ten reruns. Applying the same chain to Petri shows that it admits both tools. The substantial differences arise upstream of the chain, in claim-contract enforcement and deployment fit. A Norwegian public-sector procurement case comparing Borealis and Gemma 3 demonstrates the resulting evidence in practice: the safer model depends on scenario category and risk measure. Consequently, scores, matched deltas, critical rates, uncertainty, and the auditor and judge used must be reported together rather than collapsed into a single ranking.
中文标题/摘要
标题：当没有基准时：在没有真实标签的情况下验证比较LLM安全评分
许多部署必须在相关语言、行业或监管制度的标记基准存在之前比较候选语言模型的安全性。我们将这种情况形式化为无基准的比较安全评分，并指定场景基础审计可以被解释为部署证据的合同。分数仅在固定的场景包、评分标准、审计员、评判者、抽样配置和重跑预算下有效。由于没有可用的标签，我们用工具有效性链替代真实一致性：对受控的安全与消除对比的响应、目标驱动方差对审计员和评判者伪影的主导性，以及重跑的稳定性。我们在SimpleAudit中实例化该链，这是一个本地优先的评分工具，并在挪威安全包上验证。安全和消除目标的AUROC值在0.89到1.00之间，目标身份是主导方差成分（$η^2 \approx 0.52$），严重性轮廓在十次重跑中稳定。将相同的链应用于Petri表明它同时接受这两种工具。显著差异出现在链的上游，在索赔合同执行和部署适配中。一个比较Borealis和Gemma 3的挪威公共部门采购案例展示了实践中的证据：更安全的模型依赖于场景类别和风险度量。因此，分数、匹配的增量、关键率、不确定性以及使用的审计员和评判者必须一起报告，而不是合并为单一排名。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the challenge of evaluating language models for safety in scenarios where no labeled benchmark exists, which is crucial for various deployments. Previous methods relied on ground-truth labels for safety assessments, leading to limitations in their applicability across different languages and regulatory contexts. The proposed approach, termed benchmarkless comparative safety scoring, utilizes a scenario-based audit framework that emphasizes an instrumental-validity chain to ensure reliable scoring without ground-truth labels. This method is well-motivated as it allows for the assessment of language models based on controlled contrasts and variance stability. The paper contributes by introducing SimpleAudit, a scoring instrument validated on a Norwegian safety pack, achieving AUROC values between 0.89 and 1.00, demonstrating that the method can effectively differentiate between safe and abliterated targets while maintaining stability across multiple runs. The findings indicate that the safety scores are context-dependent, necessitating comprehensive reporting of various metrics rather than a singular ranking.
本文解决了在没有标记基准的情况下评估语言模型安全性的问题，这在各个领域的部署中至关重要。以往的方法依赖于安全评估的真实标签，这导致了其适用性和可靠性方面的局限性。所提出的方法称为无基准比较安全评分，利用基于场景的审计框架，强调了在没有真实标签的情况下验证安全评分的工具有效性链。这种方法具有良好的动机，因为它允许在缺乏传统基准的现实环境中评估语言模型。本文的贡献在于引入了SimpleAudit，一个评分工具，该工具通过挪威安全包进行了验证，AUROC值在0.89到1.00之间，并且在多次重跑中显示出稳定的严重性特征。这种方法有效支持了在缺乏既定基准的情况下提供可靠安全评估的目标。
Beyond Accuracy: Policy Invariance as a Reliability Test for LLM Safety Judges
Authors: Shihao Weng, Yang Feng, Xiaofei Xie
First: 2026-05-07T12:49:09+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-07T12:49:09+00:00
Comments: 9 pages
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
LLM-as-a-Judge pipelines have become the de facto evaluator for agent safety, yet existing benchmarks treat their verdicts as ground-truth proxies without checking whether the verdicts depend on the agent's behavior or merely on how the evaluation policy happens to be worded. We argue that any trustworthy safety judge must satisfy a basic property we call policy invariance, and we operationalize it as three testable principles: rubric-semantics invariance under certified-equivalent rewrites, rubric-threshold invariance under intentional strict-to-lenient shifts, and ambiguity-aware calibration so that verdict instability concentrates on genuinely ambiguous cases. Instantiating these principles as a stress-test protocol with four agent-class judges on trajectories drawn from ASSEBench and R-Judge, we surface a previously unmeasured failure mode: today's judges respond to meaningful normative shifts and to meaningless structural rewrites with comparable strength, and cannot tell the two apart. Content-preserving policy rewrites flip up to 9.1% of verdicts above baseline jitter, and 18-43% of all observed flips occur on unambiguous cases under such rewrites, so existing safety scores conflate what the agent did with how the evaluator was prompted. Beyond the diagnosis, we contribute the Policy Invariance Score and the Judge Card reporting protocol, which expose an order-of-magnitude spread in judge reliability that is invisible to accuracy-only leaderboards. We release the protocol and code so that future agent-safety benchmarks can audit their own evaluators rather than trust them by default.
中文标题/摘要
标题：超越准确性：政策不变性作为LLM安全评判者的可靠性测试
LLM作为评判者的管道已成为代理安全的事实评估者，但现有基准将其裁决视为真实代理，而未检查裁决是否依赖于代理的行为或仅仅依赖于评估政策的措辞。我们认为，任何值得信赖的安全评判者必须满足我们称之为政策不变性的基本属性，并将其操作化为三个可测试的原则：在经过认证的等效重写下的评分语义不变性、在有意的严格到宽松的转变下的评分阈值不变性，以及意识到模糊性的校准，以便裁决的不稳定性集中在真正模糊的案例上。将这些原则实例化为一个压力测试协议，使用来自ASSEBench和R-Judge的轨迹上的四个代理类别评判者，我们揭示了一种以前未测量的失败模式：今天的评判者对有意义的规范性变化和无意义的结构重写的反应强度相当，无法区分二者。内容保留的政策重写使得高达9.1%的裁决在基线抖动之上翻转，且在此类重写下，18-43%的所有观察到的翻转发生在明确的案例上，因此现有的安全评分混淆了代理的行为与评估者的提示方式。除了诊断，我们贡献了政策不变性评分和评判者卡报告协议，揭示了评判者可靠性在仅依赖准确性排行榜中不可见的数量级差异。我们发布了该协议和代码，以便未来的代理安全基准可以审计自己的评估者，而不是默认信任他们。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the reliability of LLM-as-a-Judge pipelines used for agent safety evaluations, highlighting that existing benchmarks often treat verdicts as accurate without verifying their dependence on agent behavior versus evaluation policy wording. Previous methods lack a systematic approach to assess this reliability, leading to potential misinterpretations of safety judgments. The proposed approach introduces the concept of policy invariance, operationalized through three testable principles that serve as a stress-test protocol for evaluating judges. This methodology reveals a significant failure mode where judges cannot distinguish between meaningful normative shifts and meaningless structural rewrites, resulting in a substantial percentage of verdict instability even in unambiguous cases. The paper contributes the Policy Invariance Score and the Judge Card reporting protocol, which provide a more nuanced understanding of judge reliability beyond mere accuracy metrics, thus supporting the goal of improving agent safety evaluations.

XL-SafetyBench: A Country-Grounded Cross-Cultural Benchmark for LLM Safety and Cultural Sensitivity
Authors: Dasol Choi, Eugenia Kim, Jaewon Noh, Sang Seo, Eunmi Kim, Myunggyo Oh, Yunjin Park, Brigitta Jesica Kartono, Josef Pichlmeier, Helena Berndt, Sai Krishna Mendu, Glenn Johannes Tungka, Özlem Gökçe, Suresh Gehlot, Katherine Pratt, Amanda Minnich, Haon Park
First: 2026-05-07T04:35:03+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-07T04:35:03+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Current LLM safety benchmarks are predominantly English-centric and often rely on translation, failing to capture country-specific harms. Moreover, they rarely evaluate a model's ability to detect culturally embedded sensitivities as distinct from universal harms. We introduce XL-SafetyBench. a suite of 5,500 test cases across 10 country-language pairs, comprising a Jailbreak Benchmark of country-grounded adversarial prompts and a Cultural Benchmark where local sensitivities are embedded within innocuous requests. Each item is constructed via a multi-stage pipeline that combines LLM-assisted discovery, automated validation gates, and dual independent native-speaker annotators per country. To distinguish principled refusal from comprehension failure, we evaluate Attack Success Rate (ASR) alongside two complementary metrics we introduce: Neutral-Safe Rate (NSR) and Cultural Sensitivity Rate (CSR). Evaluating 10 frontier and 27 local LLMs reveals two key findings. First, jailbreak robustness and cultural awareness do not show a coupled relationship among frontier models, so a composite safety score obscures per-axis variation. Second, local models exhibit a near-linear ASR-NSR trade-off (r = -0.81), indicating that their apparent safety reflects generation failure rather than genuine alignment. XL-SafetyBench enables more nuanced, cross-cultural safety evaluation in the multilingual era.
中文标题/摘要
标题：XL-SafetyBench：一个基于国家的跨文化大型语言模型安全与文化敏感性基准
当前的大型语言模型安全基准主要以英语为中心，通常依赖翻译，未能捕捉特定国家的危害。此外，它们很少评估模型检测文化嵌入敏感性与普遍危害的能力。我们推出了XL-SafetyBench，一个包含5500个测试案例的套件，涵盖10个国家-语言对，包括一个基于国家的对抗性提示的越狱基准和一个将地方敏感性嵌入无害请求中的文化基准。每个项目通过一个多阶段流程构建，该流程结合了大型语言模型辅助发现、自动验证门和每个国家的双独立母语者注释。为了区分原则性拒绝与理解失败，我们评估攻击成功率（ASR）以及我们引入的两个互补指标：中性安全率（NSR）和文化敏感性率（CSR）。对10个前沿和27个地方大型语言模型的评估揭示了两个关键发现。首先，越狱鲁棒性与文化意识在前沿模型中并不呈现耦合关系，因此复合安全评分掩盖了每个轴的变化。其次，地方模型表现出近线性的ASR-NSR权衡（r = -0.81），表明它们的表面安全反映的是生成失败而非真正的对齐。XL-SafetyBench使得在多语言时代进行更细致的跨文化安全评估成为可能。

Safety and accuracy follow different scaling laws in clinical large language models
Authors: Sebastian Wind, Tri-Thien Nguyen, Jeta Sopa, Mahshad Lotfinia, Sebastian Bickelhaup, Michael Uder, Harald Köstler, Gerhard Wellein, Sven Nebelung, Daniel Truhn, Andreas Maier, Soroosh Tayebi Arasteh
First: 2026-05-05T17:57:19+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-05T17:57:19+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Clinical LLMs are often scaled by increasing model size, context length, retrieval complexity, or inference-time compute, with the implicit expectation that higher accuracy implies safer behavior. This assumption is incomplete in medicine, where a few confident, high-risk, or evidence-contradicting errors can matter more than average benchmark performance. We introduce SaFE-Scale, a framework for measuring how clinical LLM safety changes across model scale, evidence quality, retrieval strategy, context exposure, and inference-time compute. To instantiate this framework, we introduce RadSaFE-200, a Radiology Safety-Focused Evaluation benchmark of 200 multiple-choice questions with clinician-defined clean evidence, conflict evidence, and option-level labels for high-risk error, unsafe answer, and evidence contradiction. We evaluated 34 locally deployed LLMs across six deployment conditions: closed-book prompting (zero-shot), clean evidence, conflict evidence, standard RAG, agentic RAG, and max-context prompting. Clean evidence produced the strongest improvement, increasing mean accuracy from 73.5% to 94.1%, while reducing high-risk error from 12.0% to 2.6%, contradiction from 12.7% to 2.3%, and dangerous overconfidence from 8.0% to 1.6%. Standard RAG and agentic RAG did not reproduce this safety profile: agentic RAG improved accuracy over standard RAG and reduced contradiction, but high-risk error and dangerous overconfidence remained elevated. Max-context prompting increased latency without closing the safety gap, and additional inference-time compute produced only limited gains. Worst-case analysis showed that clinically consequential errors concentrated in a small subset of questions. Clinical LLM safety is therefore not a passive consequence of scaling, but a deployment property shaped by evidence quality, retrieval design, context construction, and collective failure behavior.
中文标题/摘要
标题：临床大型语言模型中的安全性和准确性遵循不同的缩放法则
临床LLM通常通过增加模型大小、上下文长度、检索复杂性或推理时计算来进行缩放，隐含的期望是更高的准确性意味着更安全的行为。这个假设在医学中是不完整的，因为少数自信的高风险或与证据相矛盾的错误可能比平均基准表现更为重要。我们引入了SaFE-Scale，一个用于测量临床LLM安全性如何随模型规模、证据质量、检索策略、上下文暴露和推理时计算而变化的框架。为了实现这个框架，我们引入了RadSaFE-200，这是一个以放射学安全为重点的评估基准，包含200个多项选择题，具有临床医生定义的干净证据、冲突证据和高风险错误、不安全答案及证据矛盾的选项级标签。我们在六种部署条件下评估了34个本地部署的LLM：闭卷提示（零-shot）、干净证据、冲突证据、标准RAG、代理RAG和最大上下文提示。干净证据产生了最强的改进，将平均准确率从73.5%提高到94.1%，同时将高风险错误从12.0%降低到2.6%，矛盾从12.7%降低到2.3%，危险的过度自信从8.0%降低到1.6%。标准RAG和代理RAG未能重现这一安全特征：代理RAG提高了准确性并减少了矛盾，但高风险错误和危险的过度自信仍然较高。最大上下文提示增加了延迟而未缩小安全差距，额外的推理时计算仅产生有限的收益。最坏情况分析显示，临床相关错误集中在少数问题上。因此，临床LLM的安全性并不是缩放的被动结果，而是由证据质量、检索设计、上下文构建和集体失败行为所塑造的部署属性。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the inadequacy of existing methods that assume higher accuracy in clinical large language models (LLMs) equates to safer behavior, particularly in medical contexts where high-risk errors can have significant consequences. Previous approaches primarily focused on scaling model size and complexity without adequately measuring safety, leading to potential misjudgments in clinical applications. The proposed SaFE-Scale framework offers a systematic way to evaluate clinical LLM safety across various dimensions, including model scale and evidence quality, and introduces the RadSaFE-200 benchmark for assessing high-risk errors and contradictions. The methodology involved evaluating 34 LLMs under different deployment conditions, revealing that using clean evidence significantly improved accuracy and reduced high-risk errors and contradictions. The findings indicate that safety in clinical LLMs is influenced by multiple factors beyond mere scaling, highlighting the need for careful consideration of evidence and retrieval strategies in deployment.
本研究解决了现有方法的不足之处，这些方法假设临床大型语言模型（LLMs）的更高准确性等同于更安全的行为，尤其是在医疗环境中，高风险错误可能产生重大后果。以往的方法主要集中在模型规模和上下文长度的扩展，但未能考虑临床应用中安全性的复杂性。提出的SaFE-Scale框架提供了一种新颖的方法来衡量安全性，涵盖模型规模和证据质量等多个维度，并引入了RadSaFE-200基准来评估以安全为重点的性能。本研究在不同部署条件下评估了34个LLM，结果显示使用干净证据显著提高了准确性并减少了高风险错误，而标准RAG和代理RAG等其他方法未能实现同样的安全性提升。这些发现表明，临床LLM的安全性受到多个因素的影响，超越了单纯的扩展，强调在部署中对证据和检索策略的仔细考虑。
Exposing LLM Safety Gaps Through Mathematical Encoding:New Attacks and Systematic Analysis
Authors: Haoyu Zhang, Mohammad Zandsalimy, Shanu Sushmita
First: 2026-05-05T07:25:33+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-05T07:25:33+00:00
Comments: 16 pages, 2 figures, 4 tables. Accepted as a long paper at the 39th Canadian Conference on Artificial Intelligence (Canadian AI 2026)
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) employ safety mechanisms to prevent harmful outputs, yet these defenses primarily rely on semantic pattern matching. We show that encoding harmful prompts as coherent mathematical problems -- using formalisms such as set theory, formal logic, and quantum mechanics -- bypasses these filters at high rates, achieving 46%--56% average attack success across eight target models and two established benchmarks. Crucially, the effectiveness depends not on mathematical notation itself, but on whether a helper LLM deeply reformulates the harmful content into a genuine mathematical problem: rule-based encodings that apply mathematical formatting without such reformulation perform no better than unencoded baselines. We introduce a novel Formal Logic encoding that achieves attack success comparable to Set Theory, demonstrating that this vulnerability generalizes across mathematical formalisms. Additional experiments with repeat post-processing confirm that these attacks are robust to simple prompt augmentation. Notably, newer models (GPT-5, GPT-5-Mini) show substantially greater robustness than older models, though they remain vulnerable. Our findings highlight fundamental gaps in current safety frameworks and motivate defenses that reason about mathematical structure rather than surface-level semantics.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过数学编码揭示大型语言模型的安全漏洞：新攻击与系统分析
大型语言模型（LLMs）采用安全机制以防止有害输出，但这些防御主要依赖于语义模式匹配。我们展示了将有害提示编码为连贯的数学问题——使用集合论、形式逻辑和量子力学等形式主义——可以高效绕过这些过滤器，在八个目标模型和两个已建立基准上实现46%至56%的平均攻击成功率。关键在于，效果并不依赖于数学符号本身，而在于辅助LLM是否将有害内容深度重构为真正的数学问题：应用数学格式的基于规则的编码在没有这种重构的情况下表现不佳。我们引入了一种新颖的形式逻辑编码，其攻击成功率与集合论相当，证明了这种脆弱性在数学形式主义中是普遍存在的。额外的重复后处理实验确认这些攻击对简单提示增强具有鲁棒性。值得注意的是，较新的模型（GPT-5，GPT-5-Mini）显示出比旧模型更大的鲁棒性，尽管它们仍然脆弱。我们的发现突显了当前安全框架中的基本缺口，并激励针对数学结构而非表面语义进行推理的防御措施。
Summary / 总结

This study demonstrates that such encoding can bypass safety filters at rates of 46% to 56% across various models and benchmarks, particularly when a helper LLM reformulates the harmful content into a genuine mathematical problem. The paper contributes a novel Formal Logic encoding that achieves similar attack success as Set Theory, revealing a general vulnerability across mathematical formalisms. The methodology involves systematic analysis and experimentation with different encoding techniques, confirming that newer models exhibit increased robustness but remain susceptible to these attacks, thereby underscoring significant gaps in current safety frameworks and suggesting the need for defenses that consider mathematical structure.

From Prompt to Physical Actuation: Holistic Threat Modeling of LLM-Enabled Robotic Systems
Authors: Neha Nagaraja, Hayretdin Bahsi, Carlo R. da Cunha
First: 2026-04-29T23:44:07+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-04T05:54:12+00:00
Comments: Submitted to 23rd Annual International Conference on Privacy, Security, and Trust (PST2026)
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As large language models are integrated into autonomous robotic systems for task planning and control, compromised inputs or unsafe model outputs can propagate through the planning pipeline to physical-world consequences. Although prior work has studied robotic cybersecurity, adversarial perception attacks, and LLM safety independently, no existing study traces how these threat categories interact and propagate across trust boundaries in a unified architectural model. We address this gap by modeling an LLM-enabled autonomous robot in an edge-cloud architecture as a hierarchical Data Flow Diagram and applying STRIDE-per-interaction analysis across six boundary-crossing interaction points using a three-category taxonomy of Conventional Cyber Threats, Adversarial Threats, and Conversational Threats. The analysis reveals that these categories converge at the same boundary crossings, and we trace three cross-boundary attack chains from external entry points to unsafe physical actuation, each exposing a distinct architectural property: the absence of independent semantic validation between user input and actuator dispatch, cross-modal translation from visual perception to language-model instruction, and unmediated boundary crossing through provider-side tool use. To our knowledge, this is the first DFD-based threat analysis integrating all three threat categories across the full perception-planning-actuation pipeline of an LLM-enabled robotic system.
中文标题/摘要
标题：从提示到物理执行：LLM驱动机器人系统的整体威胁建模
随着大型语言模型被集成到自主机器人系统中进行任务规划和控制，受损的输入或不安全的模型输出可能会通过规划流程传播到物理世界的后果。尽管之前的研究独立地研究了机器人网络安全、对抗感知攻击和LLM安全，但尚无现有研究追踪这些威胁类别如何在统一的架构模型中相互作用和传播。我们通过将LLM驱动的自主机器人建模为边缘-云架构中的分层数据流图，并在六个跨边界交互点应用STRIDE-每次交互分析，使用常规网络威胁、对抗威胁和对话威胁的三类分类法来填补这一空白。分析表明，这些类别在相同的边界交叉处汇聚，我们追踪了三条跨边界攻击链，从外部入口点到不安全的物理执行，每条链暴露出一个独特的架构特性：用户输入与执行器调度之间缺乏独立的语义验证、从视觉感知到语言模型指令的跨模态翻译，以及通过提供方工具使用的无中介边界跨越。据我们所知，这是首个基于DFD的威胁分析，整合了所有三类威胁，覆盖了LLM驱动机器人系统的完整感知-规划-执行流程。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the integration of large language models (LLMs) into autonomous robotic systems, highlighting the potential risks associated with compromised inputs and unsafe outputs that can lead to physical-world consequences. Previous studies have examined robotic cybersecurity, adversarial perception attacks, and LLM safety in isolation, failing to explore the interactions and propagation of these threats across trust boundaries. This paper proposes a unified architectural model using a hierarchical Data Flow Diagram (DFD) and applies STRIDE-per-interaction analysis to six boundary-crossing interaction points, revealing that conventional cyber threats, adversarial threats, and conversational threats converge at these points. The findings identify three distinct attack chains that expose critical architectural vulnerabilities, including a lack of independent semantic validation and unmediated boundary crossings. This work contributes a comprehensive threat analysis framework that integrates multiple threat categories across the perception-planning-actuation pipeline of LLM-enabled robotic systems, marking a novel approach in the field.

Useless but Safe? Benchmarking Utility Recovery with User Intent Clarification in Multi-Turn Conversations
Authors: Mingqian Zheng, Malia Morgan, Liwei Jiang, Carolyn Rose, Maarten Sap
First: 2026-04-29T18:37:18+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-29T18:37:18+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Current LLM safety alignment techniques improve model robustness against adversarial attacks, but overlook whether and how LLMs can recover helpfulness when benign users clarify their intent. We introduce CarryOnBench, the first interactive benchmark that measures whether LLMs can revise their interpretation of user intent and recover utility, while remaining safe through multi-turn conversations. Starting from 398 seemingly harmful queries with benign underlying intents, we simulate 5,970 conversations by varying user follow-up sequences, evaluating 14 models on both intent-aligned utility and safety. CarryOnBench yields 1,866 different conversation flows of 4--12 turns, totaling 23,880 model responses. We design Ben-Util, a checklist-based metric that evaluates how well each model response fulfills the user's benign information need using atomic items. At turn one, models fulfill only 10.5--37.6% of the user's benign information need. When the same query includes the benign intent upfront, models fulfill 25.1--72.1%, confirming that models withhold information due to intent misinterpretation, not limited knowledge. With benign clarifications in multi-turn conversations, 13 of 14 models approach or exceed this single-turn baseline, yet recovery cost varies across models. We identify three failure modes invisible to single-turn evaluations: utility lock-in, where a model rarely updates despite clarification; unsafe recovery, where a model updates at disproportionate safety cost; and repetitive recovery, where a model recycles prior responses rather than providing new information. Moreover, conversations converge to similar harmfulness levels regardless of how conservative the model starts. These findings expose a gap that single-turn evaluations miss -- whether a model is appropriately cautious or simply unresponsive to clarified user intent.
中文标题/摘要
标题：无用但安全？在多轮对话中通过用户意图澄清基准测试实用性恢复
当前的LLM安全对齐技术提高了模型对对抗攻击的鲁棒性，但忽视了LLM在良性用户澄清意图时是否以及如何恢复有用性。我们引入CarryOnBench，这是第一个交互式基准，测量LLM在多轮对话中是否能够修正对用户意图的解释并恢复实用性，同时保持安全。从398个看似有害的查询开始，这些查询具有良性的潜在意图，我们通过变化用户后续序列模拟了5,970个对话，评估了14个模型在意图对齐的实用性和安全性方面的表现。CarryOnBench产生了1,866种不同的对话流程，轮次为4到12，总计23,880个模型响应。我们设计了Ben-Util，这是一个基于清单的指标，评估每个模型响应在多大程度上满足用户的良性信息需求。在第一轮中，模型仅满足用户良性信息需求的10.5%到37.6%。当同一查询在前面包含良性意图时，模型满足25.1%到72.1%，确认模型因意图误解而隐瞒信息，而不是知识有限。在多轮对话中，经过良性澄清，14个模型中有13个接近或超过这一单轮基准，但恢复成本在模型之间有所不同。我们识别出三种在单轮评估中不可见的失败模式：实用性锁定，即模型在澄清后很少更新；不安全恢复，即模型以不成比例的安全成本进行更新；以及重复恢复，即模型回收先前的响应而不是提供新信息。此外，无论模型起初多么保守，对话都趋向于相似的有害性水平。这些发现揭示了单轮评估所忽视的一个差距——模型是否适当地谨慎，或仅仅对澄清的用户意图无反应。

Previous methods primarily focused on single-turn evaluations, which overlook the dynamic nature of user interactions and the potential for models to misinterpret benign intents. The proposed approach, CarryOnBench, introduces an interactive benchmark that evaluates LLMs' ability to revise their understanding of user intent while maintaining safety across 5,970 simulated conversations. The findings indicate that while most models can recover utility in multi-turn settings, they exhibit varying recovery costs and encounter specific failure modes that single-turn assessments do not capture, highlighting the need for more nuanced evaluation frameworks in LLM safety and utility recovery.

Policy-Grounded Safety Evaluation of 20 Large Language Models
Authors: Juan Manuel Contreras
First: 2025-07-19T18:49:16+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-29T15:54:46+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As large language models (LLMs) become increasingly integrated into real-world applications, scalable and rigorous safety evaluation is essential. This paper introduces Aymara AI, a programmatic platform for generating and administering customized, policy-grounded safety evaluations. Aymara AI transforms natural-language safety policies into adversarial prompts and scores model responses using an AI-based rater validated against human judgments. We demonstrate its capabilities through the Aymara LLM Risk and Responsibility Matrix, which evaluates 20 commercially available LLMs across 10 real-world safety domains. Results reveal wide performance disparities, with mean safety scores ranging from 86.2% to 52.4%. While models performed well in well-established safety domains such as Misinformation (mean = 95.7%), they consistently failed in more complex or underspecified domains, notably Privacy & Impersonation (mean = 24.3%). Analyses of Variance confirmed that safety scores differed significantly across both models and domains (p < .05). These findings underscore the inconsistent and context-dependent nature of LLM safety and highlight the need for scalable, customizable tools like Aymara AI to support responsible AI development and oversight.
中文标题/摘要

The findings indicate that while models excel in established safety areas, they struggle in more complex domains, emphasizing the necessity for customizable evaluation tools to enhance responsible AI development.

Evaluating LLM Safety Under Repeated Inference via Accelerated Prompt Stress Testing
Authors: Keita Broadwater
First: 2026-02-12T10:09:13+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-28T16:38:37+00:00
Comments: 23 pages, 9 figures; editorial and LaTeX revisions for clarity; improved presentation of methodology and results; updated figures, tables, and float placement; clarified temperature sensitivity and deployment-risk analysis; expanded reporting from the same experiments; results unchanged in substance
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Traditional benchmarks for large language models (LLMs), such as HELM and AIR-BENCH, primarily assess safety through breadth-oriented evaluation across diverse tasks and risk categories. However, real-world deployment often exposes a different class of risk: operational failures that arise under repeated inference on identical or near-identical prompts rather than from broad task-level underperformance. In high-stakes settings, response consistency and safety under sustained use are therefore critical. We introduce Accelerated Prompt Stress Testing (APST), a depth-oriented evaluation framework inspired by highly accelerated stress testing in reliability engineering. APST repeatedly samples identical prompts under controlled operational conditions (such as decoding temperature) to surface latent failure modes including hallucinations, refusal inconsistency, and unsafe completions. Rather than treating failures as isolated events, APST models them as stochastic outcomes of repeated inference and uses Bernoulli and binomial formulations to estimate per-inference failure probabilities. Applying APST to multiple instruction-tuned LLMs evaluated on AIR-BENCH 2024--derived safety and security prompts, we find that models with comparable shallow-evaluation scores can exhibit substantially different empirical failure rates under repeated sampling. These results show that single-sample or low-depth evaluation can obscure meaningful differences in deployment-relevant reliability. APST complements existing benchmark methodologies by providing a practical framework for estimating failure frequency under sustained use and comparing safety reliability across models and decoding configurations.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过加速提示压力测试评估大语言模型的安全性
传统的大语言模型（LLMs）基准，如HELM和AIR-BENCH，主要通过在多样任务和风险类别中的广度评估来评估安全性。然而，实际部署往往暴露出另一类风险：在相同或近似相同的提示下重复推理所导致的操作失败，而不是广泛任务级别的表现不佳。在高风险环境中，响应一致性和持续使用下的安全性至关重要。我们引入了加速提示压力测试（APST），这是一个受可靠性工程中高度加速压力测试启发的深度评估框架。APST在受控操作条件下（如解码温度）重复采样相同的提示，以揭示潜在的失败模式，包括幻觉、拒绝不一致和不安全的完成。APST将失败视为重复推理的随机结果，并使用伯努利和二项式公式来估计每次推理的失败概率。将APST应用于多个在AIR-BENCH 2024上评估的指令调优LLMs的安全和安全提示，我们发现具有可比浅层评估分数的模型在重复采样下可能表现出显著不同的经验失败率。这些结果表明，单样本或低深度评估可能掩盖在部署相关可靠性方面的有意义差异。APST通过提供一个实用框架来估计持续使用下的失败频率，并比较模型和解码配置之间的安全可靠性，补充了现有的基准方法。
Summary / 总结
This article addresses the limitations of traditional benchmarks for large language models (LLMs), which primarily focus on broad task performance and often overlook operational failures that occur during repeated inference on similar prompts. Previous methods, such as HELM and AIR-BENCH, do not adequately capture the risks associated with sustained use, leading to a gap in understanding model reliability in real-world applications. The proposed Accelerated Prompt Stress Testing (APST) framework offers a depth-oriented evaluation approach that systematically samples identical prompts under controlled conditions to identify latent failure modes, treating failures as stochastic outcomes rather than isolated events. The contribution of this paper lies in its ability to reveal significant differences in empirical failure rates among models that appear similar in shallow evaluations, thereby enhancing the assessment of safety and reliability across various models and configurations. By applying APST to instruction-tuned LLMs, the study demonstrates that models with comparable performance can exhibit varying reliability under repeated sampling, highlighting the importance of depth-oriented evaluation in ensuring consistent safety in high-stakes settings.
本文探讨了传统大型语言模型（LLMs）安全性评估基准的局限性，这些基准通常侧重于广泛的任务表现，而忽视了在相似提示下重复推理所带来的操作风险。以往的方法，如HELM和AIR-BENCH，未能捕捉到高风险环境中响应一致性和安全性的细微差别，可能导致对关键故障模式的忽视。提出的加速提示压力测试（APST）框架提供了一种深度导向的评估方法，通过在受控条件下系统地对相同提示进行采样，以识别潜在的故障，如幻觉和不安全的完成。通过将故障建模为随机结果并采用伯努利和二项式公式，APST提供了对重复推理中故障概率的更准确估计。将APST应用于多种指令调优的LLMs，发现具有相似浅层评估分数的模型在经验故障率上存在显著差异，表明传统的低深度评估可能掩盖重要的可靠性差异。这一方法增强了现有基准，通过提供一种实用手段来评估和比较模型及配置在持续使用下的安全可靠性。
Adaptive Prompt Embedding Optimization for LLM Jailbreaking
Authors: Miles Q. Li, Benjamin C. M. Fung, Boyang Li, Radin Hamidi Rad, Ebrahim Bagheri
First: 2026-04-27T20:39:08+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-27T20:39:08+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Existing white-box jailbreak attacks against aligned LLMs typically append discrete adversarial suffixes to the user prompt, which visibly alters the prompt and operates in a combinatorial token space. Prior work has avoided directly optimizing the embeddings of the original prompt tokens, presumably because perturbing them risks destroying the prompt's semantic content. We propose Prompt Embedding Optimization (PEO), a multi-round white-box jailbreak that directly optimizes the embeddings of the original prompt tokens without appending any adversarial tokens, and show that the concern is unfounded: the optimized embeddings remain close enough to their originals that the visible prompt string is preserved exactly after nearest-token projection, and quantitative analysis shows the model's responses stay on topic for the large majority of prompts. PEO combines continuous embedding-space optimization with structured continuation targets and an adaptive failure-focused schedule. Counterintuitively, later PEO rounds can benefit from heuristic composite response scaffolds that are not natural standalone templates, yet ASR-Judge shows that the resulting gains are not merely empty formatting or scaffold-only outputs. Across two standard harmful-behavior benchmarks and competing white-box attacks spanning discrete suffix search, appended adversarial embeddings, and search-based adversarial generation, PEO outperforms all of them in our experiments.
中文标题/摘要
标题：用于大型语言模型越狱的自适应提示嵌入优化
现有针对对齐大型语言模型的白盒越狱攻击通常在用户提示后附加离散的对抗后缀，这明显改变了提示并在组合标记空间中操作。之前的工作避免直接优化原始提示标记的嵌入，可能是因为扰动它们会破坏提示的语义内容。我们提出了提示嵌入优化（PEO），这是一种多轮白盒越狱，直接优化原始提示标记的嵌入，而不附加任何对抗标记，并表明这种担忧是没有根据的：优化后的嵌入与原始嵌入保持足够接近，以至于在最近标记投影后可见的提示字符串完全保留，定量分析表明模型的响应在绝大多数提示中保持主题一致。PEO结合了连续嵌入空间优化、结构化延续目标和自适应失败聚焦调度。出乎意料的是，后期PEO轮次可以受益于并非自然独立模板的启发式复合响应支架，但ASR-Judge显示，所获得的收益不仅仅是空的格式或仅支架输出。在两个标准有害行为基准和竞争白盒攻击中，PEO在我们的实验中表现优于所有这些方法。
Summary / 总结

PEO is well-motivated as it demonstrates that the optimized embeddings can maintain semantic fidelity while enhancing the effectiveness of jailbreak attacks. Beyond Context: Large Language Models' Failure to Grasp Users' Intent
Authors: Ahmed M. Hussain, Salahuddin Salahuddin
First: 2025-12-24T11:15:57+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-24T20:27:34+00:00
Comments: 22 pages and 23 figures; updated authors list and revised manuscript
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Current Large Language Models (LLMs) safety approaches focus on explicitly harmful content while overlooking a critical vulnerability: the inability to understand context and recognize user intent. This creates exploitable vulnerabilities that malicious users can systematically leverage to circumvent safety mechanisms. We empirically evaluate multiple state-of-the-art LLMs, including ChatGPT, Claude, Gemini, and DeepSeek. Our analysis demonstrates the circumvention of reliable safety mechanisms through emotional framing, progressive revelation, and academic justification techniques. Notably, reasoning-enabled configurations amplified rather than mitigated the effectiveness of exploitation, increasing factual precision while failing to interrogate the underlying intent. The exception was Claude Opus 4.1, which prioritized intent detection over information provision in some use cases. This pattern reveals that current architectural designs create systematic vulnerabilities. These limitations require paradigmatic shifts toward contextual understanding and intent recognition as core safety capabilities rather than post-hoc protective mechanisms.
中文标题/摘要
标题：超越上下文：大型语言模型未能理解用户意图
当前大型语言模型（LLMs）的安全方法专注于显性有害内容，而忽视了一个关键漏洞：无法理解上下文和识别用户意图。这导致了恶意用户可以系统性利用的可利用漏洞，从而规避安全机制。我们对多个最先进的LLMs进行了实证评估，包括ChatGPT、Claude、Gemini和DeepSeek。我们的分析表明，通过情感框架、渐进揭示和学术辩护技术，可靠安全机制被规避。值得注意的是，启用推理的配置增强了而不是减轻了利用的有效性，提高了事实精确性，但未能质疑潜在意图。例外是Claude Opus 4.1，在某些用例中优先考虑意图检测而非信息提供。这一模式揭示了当前架构设计造成的系统性漏洞。这些局限性需要在上下文理解和意图识别方面进行范式转变，将其作为核心安全能力，而不是事后保护机制。

Logic Jailbreak: Efficiently Unlocking LLM Safety Restrictions Through Formal Logical Expression
Authors: Jingyu Peng, Maolin Wang, Nan Wang, Jiatong Li, Yuchen Li, Yuyang Ye, Wanyu Wang, Pengyue Jia, Kai Zhang, Xiangyu Zhao
First: 2025-05-18T04:23:51+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-24T07:04:26+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Despite substantial advancements in aligning large language models (LLMs) with human values, current safety mechanisms remain susceptible to jailbreak attacks. We hypothesize that this vulnerability stems from distributional discrepancies between alignment-oriented prompts and malicious prompts. To investigate this, we introduce LogiBreak, a novel and universal black-box jailbreak method that leverages logical expression translation to circumvent LLM safety systems. By converting harmful natural language prompts into formal logical expressions, LogiBreak exploits the distributional gap between alignment data and logic-based inputs, preserving the underlying semantic intent and readability while evading safety constraints. We evaluate LogiBreak on a multilingual jailbreak dataset spanning three languages, demonstrating its effectiveness across various evaluation settings and linguistic contexts.

Toward Principled LLM Safety Testing: Solving the Jailbreak Oracle Problem
Authors: Shuyi Lin, Anshuman Suri, Alina Oprea, Cheng Tan
First: 2025-06-17T20:37:29+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-24T04:36:54+00:00
Comments: Accepted to MLSys 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
As large language models (LLMs) become increasingly deployed in safety-critical applications, the lack of systematic methods to assess their vulnerability to jailbreak attacks presents a critical security gap. We introduce the jailbreak oracle problem: given a model, prompt, and decoding strategy, determine whether a jailbreak response can be generated with likelihood exceeding a specified threshold. This formalization enables a principled study of jailbreak vulnerabilities. Answering the jailbreak oracle problem poses significant computational challenges, as the search space grows exponentially with response length. We present Boa, the first system designed for efficiently solving the jailbreak oracle problem. Boa employs a two-phase search strategy: (1) breadth-first sampling to identify easily accessible jailbreaks, followed by (2) depth-first priority search guided by fine-grained safety scores to systematically explore promising yet low-probability paths. Boa enables rigorous security assessments including systematic defense evaluation, standardized comparison of red team attacks, and model certification under extreme adversarial conditions. Code is available at https://github.com/shuyilinn/BOA/tree/mlsys2026ae

AISafetyBenchExplorer: A Metric-Aware Catalogue of AI Safety Benchmarks Reveals Fragmented Measurement and Weak Benchmark Governance
Authors: Abiodun A. Solanke
First: 2026-04-14T15:26:03+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T13:27:05+00:00
Comments: This paper has been withdrawn by the author while an institutional affiliation compliance matter is under review. It may be resubmitted once the matter is resolved
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
The rapid expansion of large language model (LLM) safety evaluation has produced a substantial benchmark ecosystem, but not a correspondingly coherent measurement ecosystem. We present AISafetyBenchExplorer, a structured catalogue of 195 AI safety benchmarks released between 2018 and 2026, organized through a multi-sheet schema that records benchmark-level metadata, metric-level definitions, benchmark-paper metadata, and repository activity. This design enables meta-analysis not only of what benchmarks exist, but also of how safety is operationalized, aggregated, and judged across the literature. Using the updated catalogue, we identify a central structural problem: benchmark proliferation has outpaced measurement standardization. The current landscape is dominated by medium-complexity benchmarks (94/195), while only 7 benchmarks occupy the Popular tier. The workbook further reports strong concentration around English-only evaluation (165/195), evaluation-only resources (170/195), stale GitHub repositories (137/195), stale Hugging Face datasets (96/195), and heavy reliance on arXiv preprints among benchmarks with known venue metadata. At the metric level, the catalogue shows that familiar labels such as accuracy, F1 score, safety score, and aggregate benchmark scores often conceal materially different judges, aggregation rules, and threat models. We argue that the field's main failure mode is fragmentation rather than scarcity. Researchers now have many benchmark artifacts, but they often lack a shared measurement language, a principled basis for benchmark selection, and durable stewardship norms for post publication maintenance. AISafetyBenchExplorer addresses this gap by providing a traceable benchmark catalogue, a controlled metadata schema, and a complexity taxonomy that together support more rigorous benchmark discovery, comparison, and meta-evaluation.
中文标题/摘要
标题：AISafetyBenchExplorer：一个关注度量的AI安全基准目录揭示了分散的测量和薄弱的基准治理

Secure LLM Fine-Tuning via Safety-Aware Probing
Authors: Chengcan Wu, Zhixin Zhang, Zeming Wei, Yihao Zhang, Xiaokun Luan, Meng Sun
First: 2025-05-22T14:52:10+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T08:31:23+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) have achieved remarkable success across many applications, but their ability to generate harmful content raises serious safety concerns. Although safety alignment techniques are often applied during pre-training or post-training, recent studies show that subsequent fine-tuning on adversarial or even benign data can still compromise model safety. In this paper, we revisit the fundamental question of why fine-tuning on non-harmful data may nevertheless degrade safety. We show that the safety and task-performance loss landscapes are partially decoupled, so updates that improve task-specific performance may still move the model toward unsafe regions. Based on this insight, we propose a safety-aware probing (SAP) optimization framework for mitigating safety risks during fine-tuning. Concretely, SAP uses contrastive safety signals to locate safety-correlated directions, and optimizes a lightweight probe that perturbs hidden-state propagation during fine-tuning, thereby steering parameter updates away from harmful trajectories while preserving task-specific learning. Extensive experiments show that SAP consistently improves the safety--utility tradeoff across multiple models and tasks. Averaged over multiple LLMs, SAP reduces the harmful score significantly relative to standard fine-tuning, outperforming strong baselines while maintaining competitive task-specific performance. SAP also demonstrates stronger robustness under harmful data poisoning, adversarial fine-tuning, and a dedicated post-fine-tuning adaptive attack, validating that SAP is an effective and scalable framework for preserving LLM safety during fine-tuning. Our code is available at https://github.com/ChengcanWu/SAP.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过安全感知探测进行安全的LLM微调
大型语言模型（LLMs）在许多应用中取得了显著成功，但其生成有害内容的能力引发了严重的安全担忧。尽管安全对齐技术通常在预训练或后训练期间应用，但最近的研究表明，随后在对抗性或甚至良性数据上的微调仍可能危及模型安全。本文重新审视了一个基本问题，即为什么在无害数据上的微调仍可能降低安全性。我们表明，安全性和任务性能损失的景观部分解耦，因此改善任务特定性能的更新可能仍会使模型朝向不安全区域移动。基于这一见解，我们提出了一种安全感知探测（SAP）优化框架，以减轻微调过程中的安全风险。具体而言，SAP使用对比安全信号来定位与安全相关的方向，并优化一个轻量级探测器，在微调过程中扰动隐藏状态传播，从而将参数更新引导远离有害轨迹，同时保持任务特定学习。大量实验表明，SAP在多个模型和任务中始终改善安全性与效用的权衡。在多个LLM上平均，SAP相对于标准微调显著降低了有害评分，超越了强基线，同时保持了竞争性的任务特定性能。SAP在有害数据中毒、对抗性微调和专门的后微调自适应攻击下也表现出更强的鲁棒性，验证了SAP是一个有效且可扩展的框架，用于在微调过程中保持LLM的安全性。我们的代码可在https://github.com/ChengcanWu/SAP获取。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the safety concerns associated with large language models (LLMs), particularly how fine-tuning on non-harmful data can still lead to safety degradation. Previous methods focused on safety alignment during pre-training or post-training but failed to prevent safety risks during fine-tuning, as improvements in task performance could inadvertently push models towards unsafe regions. The proposed safety-aware probing (SAP) framework offers a novel approach by utilizing contrastive safety signals to identify safety-related directions and optimizing a lightweight probe that adjusts hidden-state propagation during fine-tuning. This method effectively mitigates safety risks while maintaining task-specific learning. The experiments demonstrate that SAP significantly enhances the safety-utility tradeoff across various models and tasks, achieving lower harmful scores compared to standard fine-tuning while preserving competitive performance, thus validating its effectiveness and scalability in ensuring LLM safety during fine-tuning.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLMs）生成有害内容所带来的安全隐患，指出传统的安全对齐技术在预训练或后训练阶段并不能完全消除微调过程中的风险。以往的方法往往未能认识到在无害数据上进行微调仍可能导致安全性下降，因为安全性和任务性能损失的景观是部分解耦的。提出的安全感知探测（SAP）框架通过利用对比安全信号来识别与安全相关的方向，并优化轻量级探测器，在微调过程中调整隐藏状态传播，从而避免有害更新，同时保持任务性能。本文的贡献在于证明SAP在多个模型和任务中显著改善了安全性与效用的权衡，相较于标准微调显著降低了有害评分，同时保持了竞争性的任务特定性能，并在有害数据中毒和对抗攻击下表现出更强的鲁棒性。
LASA: Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment at the Semantic Bottleneck for LLM Safety
Authors: Junxiao Yang, Haoran Liu, Jinzhe Tu, Jiale Cheng, Zhexin Zhang, Shiyao Cui, Jiaqi Weng, Jialing Tao, Hui Xue, Hongning Wang, Han Qiu, Minlie Huang
First: 2026-04-13T15:59:50+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T04:47:08+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) often demonstrate strong safety performance in high-resource languages, yet exhibit severe vulnerabilities when queried in low-resource languages. We attribute this gap to a mismatch between language-agnostic semantic understanding ability and language-dominant safety alignment biased toward high-resource languages. Consistent with this hypothesis, we empirically identify the semantic bottleneck in LLMs, an intermediate layer in which the geometry of model representations is governed primarily by shared semantic content rather than language identity. Building on this observation, we propose Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment (LASA), which anchors safety alignment directly in semantic bottlenecks. Experiments show that LASA substantially improves safety across all languages: average attack success rate (ASR) drops from 24.7% to 2.8% on LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct and remains around 3-4% across Qwen2.5 and Qwen3 Instruct models (7B-32B). Together, our analysis and method offer a representation-level perspective on LLM safety, suggesting that safety alignment requires anchoring safety understanding not in surface text, but in the model's language-agnostic semantic space.
中文标题/摘要
标题：LASA：在语义瓶颈处实现语言无关的语义对齐以提高大型语言模型的安全性
大型语言模型（LLMs）在高资源语言中通常表现出强大的安全性能，但在低资源语言中查询时却表现出严重的脆弱性。我们将这一差距归因于语言无关的语义理解能力与偏向高资源语言的语言主导安全对齐之间的不匹配。与这一假设一致，我们实证识别了LLMs中的语义瓶颈，这是一个中间层，其中模型表示的几何形状主要由共享的语义内容而非语言身份所主导。基于这一观察，我们提出了语言无关的语义对齐（LASA），直接在语义瓶颈中锚定安全对齐。实验表明，LASA显著提高了所有语言的安全性：在LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct上的平均攻击成功率（ASR）从24.7%降至2.8%，在Qwen2.5和Qwen3 Instruct模型（7B-32B）中保持在3-4%左右。我们的分析和方法共同提供了对LLM安全性的表示级视角，表明安全对齐需要将安全理解锚定在模型的语言无关语义空间中，而非表面文本中。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the disparity in safety performance of large language models (LLMs) between high-resource and low-resource languages, which is attributed to a mismatch in semantic understanding and safety alignment. Previous methods focused on language-specific safety measures, leading to vulnerabilities in low-resource languages. The proposed Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment (LASA) approach differs by anchoring safety alignment in the semantic bottleneck of LLMs, which is governed by shared semantic content rather than language identity. This method is well-motivated as it targets the root cause of the safety gap. The paper contributes a new perspective on LLM safety and demonstrates that LASA significantly reduces the average attack success rate from 24.7% to 2.8% on LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct and maintains low rates of 3-4% across other models, effectively supporting the goal of enhancing safety across all languages.

Dialect vs Demographics: Quantifying LLM Bias from Implicit Linguistic Signals vs. Explicit User Profiles
Authors: Irti Haq, Belén Saldías
First: 2026-04-22T23:33:18+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-22T23:33:18+00:00
Comments: In The 2026 ACM Conference on Fairness, Accountability, and Transparency (FAccT '26), June 25--28, 2026, Montreal, Canada. ACM, New York, NY, USA, 32 pages
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As state-of-the-art Large Language Models (LLMs) have become ubiquitous, ensuring equitable performance across diverse demographics is critical. However, it remains unclear whether these disparities arise from the explicitly stated identity itself or from the way identity is signaled. In real-world interactions, users' identity is often conveyed implicitly through a complex combination of various socio-linguistic factors. This study disentangles these signals by employing a factorial design with over 24,000 responses from two open-weight LLMs (Gemma-3-12B and Qwen-3-VL-8B), comparing prompts with explicitly announced user profiles against implicit dialect signals (e.g., AAVE, Singlish) across various sensitive domains. Our results uncover a unique paradox in LLM safety where users achieve ``better'' performance by sounding like a demographic than by stating they belong to it. Explicit identity prompts activate aggressive safety filters, increasing refusal rates and reducing semantic similarity compared to our reference text for Black users. In contrast, implicit dialect cues trigger a powerful ``dialect jailbreak,'' reducing refusal probability to near zero while simultaneously achieving a greater level of semantic similarity to the reference texts compared to Standard American English prompts. However, this ``dialect jailbreak'' introduces a critical safety trade-off regarding content sanitization. We find that current safety alignment techniques are brittle and over-indexed on explicit keywords, creating a bifurcated user experience where ``standard'' users receive cautious, sanitized information while dialect speakers navigate a less sanitized, more raw, and potentially a more hostile information landscape and highlights a fundamental tension in alignment--between equitable and linguistic diversity--and underscores the need for safety mechanisms that generalize beyond explicit cues.

标题：方言与人口统计：量化隐性语言信号与显性用户档案中的LLM偏见
随着最先进的大型语言模型（LLMs）变得无处不在，确保在不同人口统计中公平的表现至关重要。然而，这些差异是否源于明确声明的身份本身，还是身份信号的方式仍不清楚。在现实互动中，用户的身份通常通过各种社会语言因素的复杂组合隐性传达。本研究通过采用因子设计，利用来自两个开放权重LLM（Gemma-3-12B和Qwen-3-VL-8B）的超过24,000个响应，解开这些信号，比较显性用户档案的提示与隐性方言信号（例如，AAVE，Singlish）在各种敏感领域的表现。我们的结果揭示了LLM安全性中的一个独特悖论，即用户通过听起来像某个群体而不是明确声明自己属于该群体来获得“更好”的表现。显性身份提示激活了激进的安全过滤器，增加了拒绝率，并减少了与黑人用户参考文本的语义相似性。相比之下，隐性方言线索触发了强大的“方言越狱”，将拒绝概率降低到接近零，同时在与标准美式英语提示相比时，达到更高的语义相似性。然而，这种“方言越狱”引入了关于内容净化的关键安全权衡。我们发现当前的安全对齐技术脆弱，并过度依赖显性关键词，造成了“标准”用户接收谨慎、净化的信息，而方言使用者则在一个较少净化、更原始且可能更具敌意的信息环境中导航，突显了对齐中的基本紧张关系——在公平性与语言多样性之间——并强调了需要超越显性线索的安全机制。

LLM Safety From Within: Detecting Harmful Content with Internal Representations
Authors: Difan Jiao, Yilun Liu, Ye Yuan, Zhenwei Tang, Linfeng Du, Haolun Wu, Ashton Anderson
First: 2026-04-20T17:17:07+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-20T17:17:07+00:00
Comments: 17 pages,10 figures,6 tables
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Guard models are widely used to detect harmful content in user prompts and LLM responses. However, state-of-the-art guard models rely solely on terminal-layer representations and overlook the rich safety-relevant features distributed across internal layers. We present SIREN, a lightweight guard model that harnesses these internal features. By identifying safety neurons via linear probing and combining them through an adaptive layer-weighted strategy, SIREN builds a harmfulness detector from LLM internals without modifying the underlying model. Our comprehensive evaluation shows that SIREN substantially outperforms state-of-the-art open-source guard models across multiple benchmarks while using 250 times fewer trainable parameters. Moreover, SIREN exhibits superior generalization to unseen benchmarks, naturally enables real-time streaming detection, and significantly improves inference efficiency compared to generative guard models. Overall, our results highlight LLM internal states as a promising foundation for practical, high-performance harmfulness detection.

Different Paths to Harmful Compliance: Behavioral Side Effects and Mechanistic Divergence Across LLM Jailbreaks
Authors: Md Rysul Kabir, Zoran Tiganj
First: 2026-04-20T17:01:27+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-20T17:01:27+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Open-weight language models can be rendered unsafe through several distinct interventions, but the resulting models may differ substantially in capabilities, behavioral profile, and internal failure mode. We study behavioral and mechanistic properties of jailbroken models across three unsafe routes: harmful supervised fine-tuning (SFT), harmful reinforcement learning with verifiable rewards (RLVR), and refusal-suppressing abliteration. All three routes achieve near-ceiling harmful compliance, but they diverge once we move beyond direct harmfulness. RLVR-jailbroken models show minimal degradation and preserve explicit harm recognition in a structured self-audit: they are able to identify harmful prompts and describe how a safe LLM should respond, yet they comply with the harmful request. With RLVR, harmful behavior is strongly suppressed by a reflective safety scaffold: when a harmful prompt is prepended with an instruction to reflect on safety standards, harmful behavior drops close to the baseline. Category-specific RLVR jailbreaks generalize broadly across harmfulness domains. Models jailbroken with SFT show the largest collapse in explicit safety judgments, the highest behavioral drift, and a substantial capability loss on standard benchmarks. Abliteration is family-dependent in both self-audit and response to a reflective safety scaffold. Mechanistic and repair analyses further separate the routes: abliteration is consistent with localized refusal-feature deletion, RLVR with preserved safety geometry but retargeted policy behavior, and SFT with broader distributed drift. Targeted repair partially recovers RLVR-jailbroken models, but has little effect on SFT-jailbroken models. Together, these results show that jailbreaks can produce vastly different properties despite similar harmfulness, with models jailbroken via RLVR showing remarkable similarity to the base model.
中文标题/摘要
标题：有害合规的不同路径：行为副作用和大型语言模型越狱的机制差异
开放权重语言模型可以通过几种不同的干预措施变得不安全，但结果模型在能力、行为特征和内部故障模式上可能有显著差异。我们研究了通过三种不安全路径越狱模型的行为和机制特性：有害的监督微调（SFT）、有害的可验证奖励强化学习（RLVR）和拒绝抑制消融。这三条路径都实现了接近上限的有害合规，但一旦超越直接的有害性，它们就会出现分歧。RLVR越狱模型表现出最小的退化，并在结构化自我审计中保持明确的有害识别：它们能够识别有害提示并描述安全大型语言模型应如何响应，但仍然遵从有害请求。通过RLVR，有害行为在反思安全框架下被强烈抑制：当有害提示前面加上反思安全标准的指令时，有害行为接近基线。特定类别的RLVR越狱在有害性领域广泛泛化。通过SFT越狱的模型在明确的安全判断上出现最大崩溃，行为漂移最高，并在标准基准上有显著能力损失。消融在自我审计和对反思安全框架的响应中依赖于家庭。机制和修复分析进一步区分了这些路径：消融与局部拒绝特征删除一致，RLVR与保留的安全几何但重新定向的政策行为一致，SFT则表现出更广泛的分布漂移。针对性修复部分恢复了RLVR越狱模型，但对SFT越狱模型影响不大。综合来看，这些结果表明，尽管有害性相似，越狱可以产生截然不同的特性，RLVR越狱模型与基础模型表现出显著相似性。
Summary / 总结
This research investigates the behavioral and mechanistic differences among various methods of rendering open-weight language models unsafe, specifically focusing on harmful supervised fine-tuning (SFT), harmful reinforcement learning with verifiable rewards (RLVR), and refusal-suppressing abliteration. Previous methods often resulted in models that exhibited significant degradation in safety judgments and behavioral drift, particularly with SFT, which led to a loss of capabilities. The proposed approach, particularly RLVR, addresses these issues by maintaining explicit harm recognition and allowing models to reflect on safety standards, thus achieving near-ceiling harmful compliance while minimizing harmful behavior. The study contributes to understanding the distinct pathways to harmful compliance and their implications for model safety. The methodology involves analyzing the performance of jailbroken models across various tasks, revealing that RLVR models retain more capabilities and safety features compared to those modified by SFT, supporting the goal of developing safer AI systems.

StealthGraph: Exposing Domain-Specific Risks in LLMs through Knowledge-Graph-Guided Harmful Prompt Generation
Authors: Huawei Zheng, Xinqi Jiang, Sen Yang, Shouling Ji, Yingcai Wu, Dazhen Deng
First: 2026-01-08T09:05:28+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-20T15:12:04+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) are increasingly applied in specialized domains such as finance and healthcare, where they introduce unique safety risks. Domain-specific datasets of harmful prompts remain scarce and still largely rely on manual construction; public datasets mainly focus on explicit harmful prompts, which modern LLM defenses can often detect and refuse. In contrast, implicit harmful prompts-expressed through indirect domain knowledge-are harder to detect and better reflect real-world threats. We identify two challenges: transforming domain knowledge into actionable constraints and increasing the implicitness of generated harmful prompts. To address them, we propose an end-to-end framework that first performs knowledge-graph-guided harmful prompt generation to systematically produce domain-relevant prompts, and then applies two-strategy obfuscation rewriting to convert explicit harmful prompts into implicit variants via direct and context-enhanced rewriting. This framework yields high-quality datasets combining strong domain relevance with implicitness, enabling more realistic red-teaming and advancing LLM safety research. We release our code and datasets on GitHub.
中文标题/摘要
标题：StealthGraph：通过知识图谱引导的有害提示生成揭示大型语言模型中的特定领域风险
大型语言模型（LLMs）越来越多地应用于金融和医疗等专业领域，这些领域引入了独特的安全风险。有害提示的特定领域数据集仍然稀缺，且主要依赖手动构建；公共数据集主要集中在显性有害提示上，而现代LLM防御通常可以检测并拒绝这些提示。相比之下，通过间接领域知识表达的隐性有害提示更难以检测，更能反映现实世界的威胁。我们识别出两个挑战：将领域知识转化为可操作的约束，以及增加生成有害提示的隐性程度。为了解决这些问题，我们提出了一个端到端框架，首先进行知识图谱引导的有害提示生成，以系统性地生成与领域相关的提示，然后应用双策略模糊重写，将显性有害提示通过直接和上下文增强重写转换为隐性变体。该框架生成的高质量数据集结合了强领域相关性和隐性，能够实现更现实的红队测试并推动LLM安全研究。我们将在GitHub上发布我们的代码和数据集。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the safety risks posed by large language models (LLMs) in specialized domains like finance and healthcare, where existing methods for generating harmful prompts are limited by a reliance on manual construction and focus primarily on explicit prompts that are easily detectable. The proposed approach, StealthGraph, differs by utilizing a knowledge-graph-guided framework to systematically generate domain-relevant harmful prompts and employing obfuscation rewriting strategies to convert explicit prompts into more implicit forms, thus enhancing realism in threat modeling. This paper contributes a novel methodology that produces high-quality datasets characterized by strong domain relevance and implicitness, which supports more effective red-teaming efforts and advances the field of LLM safety research. The methodology demonstrates effectiveness in generating realistic harmful prompts, thereby addressing the identified challenges and supporting the goals of improving LLM safety.

Uncovering Logit Suppression Vulnerabilities in LLM Safety Alignment
Authors: Yuxi Li, Yi Liu, Yuekang Li, Ling Shi, Gelei Deng, Shengquan Chen, Kailong Wang
First: 2024-05-20T17:17:55+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-18T08:25:50+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) have revolutionized various applications, making robust safety alignment essential to prevent harmful outputs. Current safety alignment techniques, however, harbor inherent vulnerabilities due to their reliance on logit suppression. In this work, we identify critical logit-level vulnerabilities by introducing Semantic-sensitive Alignment and Generation (SSAG), a method designed to systematically manipulate output-layer logits without altering model parameters. Experiments on five popular LLMs show that SSAG exposes harmful responses with a 95% success rate while reducing response time by 86%. VulMine also demonstrates superior attack efficacy, achieving an average ASR of up to 77% against strong defensive mechanisms. These findings reveal crucial weaknesses in existing alignment methods, highlighting an urgent need for improved vulnerability detection and robust safety alignment strategies. Our code is available on github.
中文标题/摘要
标题：揭示大型语言模型安全对齐中的逻辑抑制漏洞
大型语言模型（LLMs）已彻底改变了各种应用，使得强健的安全对齐成为防止有害输出的关键。然而，当前的安全对齐技术由于依赖逻辑抑制而存在固有漏洞。在本研究中，我们通过引入语义敏感对齐与生成（SSAG）方法，识别出关键的逻辑级漏洞，该方法旨在系统性地操控输出层逻辑而不改变模型参数。在五个流行的LLM上进行的实验表明，SSAG以95%的成功率揭示了有害响应，同时将响应时间减少了86%。VulMine还展示了卓越的攻击效果，对强防御机制的平均攻击成功率（ASR）高达77%。这些发现揭示了现有对齐方法中的关键弱点，突显了改进漏洞检测和强健安全对齐策略的迫切需求。我们的代码可在github上获取。

Previous methods have not effectively identified these vulnerabilities, prompting the introduction of Semantic-sensitive Alignment and Generation (SSAG), which manipulates output-layer logits without changing model parameters. ReGA: Model-Based Safeguard for LLMs via Representation-Guided Abstraction
Authors: Zeming Wei, Chengcan Wu, Meng Sun
First: 2025-06-02T15:17:38+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-18T05:40:12+00:00
Comments: FSE 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large Language Models (LLMs) have achieved tremendous success in various tasks, yet concerns about their safety and security have emerged. In particular, they pose risks of generating harmful content and are vulnerable to jailbreaking attacks, creating unaddressed security issues regarding their deployments. In the context of software engineering for artificial intelligence (SE4AI) techniques, model-based analysis has demonstrated notable potential for analyzing and monitoring machine learning models, particularly in stateful deep neural networks. However, it suffers from scalability issues when extended to LLMs due to their vast feature spaces. In this paper, we aim to address the scalability issue of model-based analysis techniques for safeguarding LLM-scale models. Motivated by the recent discovery of low-dimensional safety-critical representations that emerged in LLMs, we propose ReGA, a model-based analysis framework with Representation-Guided Abstraction, to safeguard LLMs against harmful prompts and generations. By leveraging safety-critical representations, which are key directions in hidden states that indicate safety-related concepts, ReGA effectively narrows the scalability gap when developing the abstract model for safety modeling. Our comprehensive evaluation shows that ReGA performs sufficiently well in distinguishing between safe and harmful inputs, achieving an AUROC of 0.975 at the prompt level and 0.985 at the conversation level. Additionally, ReGA exhibits robustness to real-world attacks and generalization across different safety perspectives, outperforming existing safeguard paradigms in terms of interpretability and scalability. Overall, ReGA serves as an efficient and scalable solution to enhance LLM safety by integrating representation engineering with model-based abstraction, paving the way for new paradigms to utilize software insights for AI safety.
中文标题/摘要
标题：ReGA：基于模型的LLM安全保障通过表示引导抽象
大型语言模型（LLMs）在各种任务中取得了巨大的成功，但也出现了关于其安全性和保障的担忧。特别是，它们存在生成有害内容的风险，并且容易受到越狱攻击，导致其部署存在未解决的安全问题。在人工智能软件工程（SE4AI）技术的背景下，基于模型的分析在分析和监控机器学习模型方面显示出显著潜力，特别是在有状态的深度神经网络中。然而，当扩展到LLMs时，由于其庞大的特征空间，它面临可扩展性问题。本文旨在解决基于模型的分析技术在保护LLM规模模型时的可扩展性问题。受到最近发现的在LLMs中出现的低维安全关键表示的启发，我们提出了ReGA，一个基于模型的分析框架，采用表示引导抽象，以保护LLMs免受有害提示和生成的影响。通过利用安全关键表示，这些表示是指示安全相关概念的隐藏状态中的关键方向，ReGA有效缩小了在安全建模中开发抽象模型时的可扩展性差距。我们的综合评估表明，ReGA在区分安全和有害输入方面表现良好，在提示级别上实现了0.975的AUROC，在对话级别上实现了0.985。此外，ReGA对现实世界攻击表现出鲁棒性，并在不同安全视角下具有良好的泛化能力，在可解释性和可扩展性方面超越了现有的安全保障范式。总体而言，ReGA通过将表示工程与基于模型的抽象相结合，作为一种高效且可扩展的解决方案，增强了LLM的安全性，为利用软件洞察力提升AI安全开辟了新范式。

SafeDream: Safety World Model for Proactive Early Jailbreak Detection
Authors: Bo Yan, Weikai Lin, Yada Zhu, Song Wang
First: 2026-04-18T04:31:33+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-18T04:31:33+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Multi-turn jailbreak attacks progressively erode LLM safety alignment across seemingly innocuous conversation turns, achieving success rates exceeding 90% against state-of-the-art models. Existing alignment-based and guardrail methods suffer from three key limitations: they require costly weight modification, evaluate each turn independently without modeling cumulative safety erosion, and detect attacks only after harmful content has been generated. To address these limitations, we first formulate the proactive early jailbreak detection problem with a new metric, detection lead, that measures how early an attack can be detected before the LLM complies. We then propose SAFEDREAM, a lightweight world-model-based framework that operates as an external module without modifying the LLM's weights. SAFEDREAM introduces three components: (1) a safety state world model that encodes LLM hidden states into a compact safety representation and predicts how it evolves across turns, (2) CUSUM detection that accumulates weak per-turn risk signals into reliable evidence, and (3) contrastive imagination that simultaneously rolls out attack and benign futures in latent space to issue early alarms before jailbreaks occur. On three multi-turn jailbreak benchmarks (XGuard-Train, SafeDialBench, SafeMTData) against 8 baselines, SAFEDREAM achieves the best detection timeliness across all benchmarks (1.06-1.20 turns before compliance) while maintaining competitive false positive rates and outperforming baselines in detection quality.
中文标题/摘要
标题：SafeDream：主动早期越狱检测的安全世界模型
多轮越狱攻击逐步侵蚀大型语言模型（LLM）的安全对齐，在看似无害的对话轮次中成功率超过90%，针对最先进的模型。现有的基于对齐和护栏的方法存在三个主要局限性：需要昂贵的权重修改，独立评估每个轮次而不建模累积的安全侵蚀，并且仅在生成有害内容后检测攻击。为了解决这些局限性，我们首先用一个新的指标——检测提前量，来制定主动早期越狱检测问题，该指标衡量攻击在LLM遵从之前可以被检测的早期程度。然后，我们提出了SAFEDREAM，一个轻量级的基于世界模型的框架，作为外部模块运行，而不修改LLM的权重。SAFEDREAM引入了三个组件：（1）安全状态世界模型，将LLM的隐藏状态编码为紧凑的安全表示，并预测其在轮次中的演变；（2）CUSUM检测，将每轮的微弱风险信号累积为可靠证据；（3）对比想象，同时在潜在空间中展开攻击和良性未来，以在越狱发生之前发出早期警报。在三个多轮越狱基准（XGuard-Train、SafeDialBench、SafeMTData）上，SAFEDREAM在所有基准中实现了最佳检测及时性（在遵从之前1.06-1.20轮），同时保持竞争性的假阳性率，并在检测质量上超越基线。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the growing concern of multi-turn jailbreak attacks that compromise the safety alignment of large language models (LLMs), achieving over 90% success rates against leading models. Previous methods, including alignment-based and guardrail approaches, face significant limitations such as the need for expensive weight modifications, independent evaluation of conversation turns without considering cumulative safety erosion, and the inability to detect attacks until harmful content is generated. The proposed method, SAFEDREAM, is motivated by the need for proactive early detection and introduces a world-model-based framework that operates externally without altering LLM weights. It comprises a safety state world model, CUSUM detection for accumulating risk signals, and contrastive imagination for predicting potential attack scenarios. SAFEDREAM demonstrates superior performance on three multi-turn jailbreak benchmarks, achieving the best detection timeliness by identifying attacks 1.06 to 1.20 turns before compliance while maintaining competitive false positive rates and enhancing detection quality compared to existing baselines.

SafeLM: Unified Privacy-Aware Optimization for Trustworthy Federated Large Language Models
Authors: Noor Islam S. Mohammad, Uluğ Bayazıt
First: 2026-04-17T18:00:58+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-17T18:00:58+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) are increasingly deployed in high-stakes domains, yet a unified treatment of their overlapping safety challenges remains lacking. We present SafeLM, a framework that jointly addresses four pillars of LLM safety: privacy, security, misinformation, and adversarial robustness. SafeLM combines federated training with gradient smartification and Paillier encryption for privacy, integrates defenses against training and inference-time attacks, employs contrastive grounding with calibrated decoding to reduce hallucinations, and introduces alignment-aware binarized aggregation to enhance robustness while maintaining bounded reconstruction quality. Across benchmarks on factuality, toxicity, and membership inference, SafeLM achieves 98.0% harmful content detection accuracy, reduces communication by 96.9%, and lowers gradient inversion PSNR from 31.7 dB to 15.1 dB. Ablations show that each component contributes independently, whereas their integration yields a strong privacy utility efficiency trade-off for deploying trustworthy LLMs.
中文标题/摘要
标题：SafeLM：可信联邦大型语言模型的统一隐私意识优化
大型语言模型（LLMs）越来越多地应用于高风险领域，但对其重叠安全挑战的统一处理仍然缺乏。我们提出了SafeLM，一个共同解决LLM安全四大支柱的框架：隐私、安全、错误信息和对抗鲁棒性。SafeLM结合了联邦训练、梯度智能化和Paillier加密以保护隐私，整合了针对训练和推理时攻击的防御，采用对比基础与校准解码以减少幻觉，并引入对齐感知的二元聚合以增强鲁棒性，同时保持有限的重建质量。在事实性、有害性和成员推断的基准测试中，SafeLM实现了98.0%的有害内容检测准确率，减少了96.9%的通信量，并将梯度反演PSNR从31.7 dB降低到15.1 dB。消融实验表明，每个组件独立贡献，而它们的整合为部署可信的LLM提供了强大的隐私效用效率权衡。
